class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Hudson Bay</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>\n<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">A large body of saltwater in northeastern Canada that drains much of north-central North America</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For the outlet of the Hudson River, see <a href="/wiki/New_York_Harbor" title="New York Harbor">New York Harbor</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay_(disambiguation)" title="Hudson Bay (disambiguation)">Hudson Bay (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<table class="infobox vcard" scope="row">Settlements</th><td><a href="/wiki/Churchill,_Manitoba" title="Churchill, Manitoba">Churchill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sanikiluaq" title="Sanikiluaq">Sanikiluaq</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Hudson Bay</b> (<a href="/wiki/Inuktitut" title="Inuktitut">Inuktitut</a>: <i>Kangiqsualuk ilua</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">baie d\'Hudson</i>) (sometimes called <b>Hudson\'s Bay</b>, usually historically) is a large body of saltwater in northeastern <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> with a surface area of  1,230,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (470,000&#160;sq&#160;mi). It <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay_drainage_basin" title="Hudson Bay drainage basin">drains a very large area</a>, about 3,861,400&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1,490,900&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlas_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-atlas-3">[3]</a></sup> that includes parts of southeastern <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan" title="Saskatchewan">Saskatchewan</a>, most of <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> and indirectly through smaller passages of water to parts of <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>. Hudson Bay\'s southern arm is called <a href="/wiki/James_Bay" title="James Bay">James Bay</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cree_language" title="Cree language">Eastern Cree</a> name for Hudson and James Bay is <i>W&#238;nipekw</i> (Southern dialect) or <i>W&#238;nip&#226;kw</i> (Northern dialect), meaning muddy or brackish water. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Winnipeg" title="Lake Winnipeg">Lake Winnipeg</a> is similarly named by the local <a href="/wiki/Cree" title="Cree">Cree</a>, as is the location for the city of <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg" title="Winnipeg">Winnipeg</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span tocsection-11"><a href="#Arctic_Bridge"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Arctic Bridge</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Coastal_communities"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Coastal communities</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Military_development"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Military development</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Description">Description</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Description">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hudson-bassin.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="230" data-file-width="280" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Hudson-bassin.PNG/220px-Hudson-bassin.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/Hudson-bassin.PNG 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hudson-bassin.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay_drainage_basin" title="Hudson Bay drainage basin">Hudson Bay drainage basin</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The bay is named after <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">Henry Hudson</a>, an Englishman sailing for the Dutch East India Company, and after whom <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">the river that he explored in 1609 is also named</a>. Hudson Bay encompasses 1,230,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (470,000&#160;sq&#160;mi), making it the second-largest water body using the term "bay" in the world (after the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a>). The bay is relatively shallow and is considered an <a href="/wiki/Inland_sea_(geology)" title="Inland sea (geology)">epicontinental sea</a>, with an average depth of about 100&#160;m (330&#160;ft) (compared to 2,600&#160;m (8,500&#160;ft) in the Bay of Bengal). It is about 1,370&#160;km (850&#160;mi) long and 1,050&#160;km (650&#160;mi) wide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> On the east it is connected with the Atlantic Ocean by <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Strait" title="Hudson Strait">Hudson Strait</a>; on the north, with the Arctic Ocean by <a href="/wiki/Foxe_Basin" title="Foxe Basin">Foxe Basin</a> (which is not considered part of the bay), and <a href="/wiki/Fury_and_Hecla_Strait" title="Fury and Hecla Strait">Fury and Hecla Strait</a>.\n</p><p>Hudson Bay is often considered part of the Arctic Ocean; the <a href="/wiki/International_Hydrographic_Organization" title="International Hydrographic Organization">International Hydrographic Organization</a>, in its 2002 working draft<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> of <i>Limits of Oceans and Seas</i>) defined the Hudson Bay, with its outlet extending from 62.5 to 66.5 degrees north (just a few miles south of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Circle" title="Arctic Circle">Arctic Circle</a>) as being part of the Arctic Ocean, specifically "Arctic Ocean Subdivision 9.11."  Other authorities include it in the Atlantic, in part because of its greater water budget connection with that ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LewisJones2000_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-LewisJones2000-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McColl2005_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-McColl2005-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EarleGlover2008_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-EarleGlover2008-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reddy2001_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reddy2001-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DayGarratt2006_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-DayGarratt2006-10">[10]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some sources describe Hudson Bay as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marginal_sea" title="Marginal sea">marginal sea</a> of the Atlantic Ocean,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calow1999_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Calow1999-11">[11]</a></sup> or the Arctic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wright2001_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wright2001-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Canada treats the bay as an <a href="/wiki/Internal_waters" title="Internal waters">internal body of water</a> and has claimed it as such on historic grounds. This claim is disputed by the United States but no action to resolve it has been taken.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hudson_bay_explorer.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="442" data-file-width="550" decoding="async" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Hudson_bay_explorer.png/220px-Hudson_bay_explorer.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Hudson_bay_explorer.png/330px-Hudson_bay_explorer.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Hudson_bay_explorer.png/440px-Hudson_bay_explorer.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hudson_bay_explorer.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Canada, Routes of Explorers, 1497 to 1905</div></div></div>\n<p>English explorers and colonists named Hudson Bay after <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">Sir Henry Hudson</a> who explored the bay beginning August 2, 1610 on his ship <i><a href="/wiki/Discovery_(1602_ship)" title="Discovery (1602 ship)">Discovery</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Butts2009_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Butts2009-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>170</span></sup> On his fourth voyage to North America, Hudson worked his way around <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>\'s west coast and into the bay, mapping much of its eastern coast. <i>Discovery</i> became trapped in the ice over the winter, and the crew survived onshore at the southern tip of James Bay. When the ice cleared in the spring, Hudson wanted to explore the rest of the area, but the crew <a href="/wiki/Mutiny" title="Mutiny">mutinied</a> on June 22, 1611. They left Hudson and others adrift in a small boat. No one knows the fate of Hudson or the crew members stranded with him, but historians see no evidence that they survived for long afterwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Butts2009_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Butts2009-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>185</span></sup>\n</p><p>In 1668, <i><a href="/wiki/Nonsuch_(1650_ship)" title="Nonsuch (1650 ship)">Nonsuch</a></i> reached the bay and traded for <a href="/wiki/North_American_beaver" title="North American beaver">beaver</a> pelts, leading to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company" title="Hudson\'s Bay Company">Hudson\'s Bay Company</a> (HBC) which still bears the historic name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The HBC negotiated a trading monopoly from the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English crown</a> for the Hudson Bay <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">watershed</a>, called <a href="/wiki/Rupert%27s_Land" title="Rupert\'s Land">Rupert\'s Land</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Galbraith1957_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Galbraith1957-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> France contested this grant by sending <a href="/wiki/List_of_Anglo-French_conflicts_on_Hudson_Bay" title="List of Anglo-French conflicts on Hudson Bay">several military expeditions</a> to the region, but abandoned its claim in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> (April 1713).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During this period, the Hudson\'s Bay Company built several <a href="/wiki/Factory_(trading_post)" title="Factory (trading post)">factories</a> (<a href="/wiki/Fortification" title="Fortification">forts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading posts</a>) along the coast at the mouth of the major rivers (such as <a href="/wiki/Fort_Severn_First_Nation" title="Fort Severn First Nation">Fort Severn, Ontario</a>; <a href="/wiki/York_Factory" title="York Factory">York Factory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Churchill,_Manitoba" title="Churchill, Manitoba">Churchill, Manitoba</a>). The strategic locations were bases for inland exploration. More importantly, they were trading posts with the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Canada" title="Indigenous peoples in Canada">indigenous peoples</a> who came to them with furs from their trapping season. The HBC shipped the furs to Europe and continued to use some of these posts well into the 20th century. The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Churchill" title="Port of Churchill">Port of Churchill</a> was an important shipping link for trade with Europe and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> until its closure in 2016 by owner <a href="/wiki/OmniTRAX" title="OmniTRAX">OmniTRAX</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p><p>HBC\'s trade monopoly was abolished in 1870, and it <a href="/wiki/Rupert%27s_Land_Act_1868" title="Rupert\'s Land Act 1868">ceded Rupert\'s Land</a> to Canada, an area of approximately 3,900,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1,500,000&#160;sq&#160;mi), as part of the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Galbraith1957_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Galbraith1957-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>427</span></sup> Starting in 1913, the Bay was extensively charted by the Canadian Government\'s <a href="/wiki/CSS_Acadia" title="CSS Acadia">CSS&#160;<i>Acadia</i></a> to develop it for navigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> This mapping progress led to the establishment of Churchill, Manitoba as a deep-sea port for wheat exports in 1929, after unsuccessful attempts at <a href="/wiki/Port_Nelson,_Manitoba" title="Port Nelson, Manitoba">Port Nelson</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extent">Extent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Extent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Hydrographic_Organization" title="International Hydrographic Organization">International Hydrographic Organization</a> defines the northern limit of Hudson Bay as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>A line from <a href="/wiki/Nuvuk_Islands" title="Nuvuk Islands">Nuvuk Point</a> (<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Hudson_Bay&amp;params=62_21_N_78_06_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">62&#176;21&#8242;N</span> <span class="longitude">78&#176;06&#8242;W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">62.350&#176;N 78.100&#176;W</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">62.350; -78.100</span></span></span></a></span>) to Leyson Point, the Southeastern extreme of <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Island" title="Southampton Island">Southampton Island</a>, through the Southern and Western shores of Southampton Island to its Northern extremity, thence a line to Beach Point (<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Hudson_Bay&amp;params=66_03_N_86_06_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">66&#176;03&#8242;N</span> <span class="longitude">86&#176;06&#8242;W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">66.050&#176;N 86.100&#176;W</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">66.050; -86.100</span></span></span></a></span>) on the Mainland.\n</p></blockquote>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ursus_maritimus_walks_over_ice.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ursus_maritimus_walks_over_ice.jpg/220px-Ursus_maritimus_walks_over_ice.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ursus_maritimus_walks_over_ice.jpg/330px-Ursus_maritimus_walks_over_ice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ursus_maritimus_walks_over_ice.jpg/440px-Ursus_maritimus_walks_over_ice.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ursus_maritimus_walks_over_ice.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Polar bear walks on newly formed ice in early November at Hudson Bay.</div></div></div>\n<p>North of Hudson Bay has a <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">polar climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen</a>: <i>ET</i>) being one of the few places in the world where this type of climate is found south of 60 &#176;N, going further south towards <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Inukjuak" title="Inukjuak">Inukjuak</a> is still dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a>. From <a href="/wiki/Arviat" title="Arviat">Arviat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a> to the west to the south and southeast prevails the <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen</a>: <i>Dfc</i>). This is because in the central summer months, heat waves can advance and leave the weather cool, where the average temperature of the month is above 10 &#176;C. At the southern end in the extension known as <a href="/wiki/James_Bay" title="James Bay">James Bay</a> arises the <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> with a more pronounced and hot summer. (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen</a>: <i>Dfb</i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The average annual temperature in almost the entire bay is around 0 &#176; C or below. Except for the <a href="/wiki/James_Bay" title="James Bay">James Bay</a> area the average water temperature is only 7&#176; C to the south in January. Although the difference is small in summer in the extreme northeast, wintery temperatures are four to five colder degrees coming near -27 &#176;C.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Hudson Bay region has very low year-round average temperatures. The average annual temperature for Churchill at <a href="/wiki/59th_parallel_north" title="59th parallel north">59&#176;N</a> is &#8722;5&#160;&#176;C (23&#160;&#176;F) and Inukjuak facing cool westerlies in summer at <a href="/wiki/58th_parallel_north" title="58th parallel north">58&#176;N</a> an even colder &#8722;7&#160;&#176;C (19&#160;&#176;F); by comparison <a href="/wiki/Arkhangelsk" title="Arkhangelsk">Arkhangelsk</a> at <a href="/wiki/64th_parallel_north" title="64th parallel north">64&#176;N</a> with a similar <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a> in northern Russia has an average of 2&#160;&#176;C (36&#160;&#176;F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>) and the mild continental coastline of Stockholm at 59&#176;N at near 8&#160;&#176;C (46&#160;&#176;F) on the seashore of a similar inlet major body of water; the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Water temperature peaks at 8&#8211;9&#160;&#176;C (46&#8211;48&#160;&#176;F) on the western side of the bay in late summer. It is largely frozen over from mid-December to mid-June when it usually clears from its eastern end westwards and southwards. A steady increase in regional temperatures over the last 100 years has been reflected in a lengthening of the ice-free period which was as short as four months in the late 17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="width:100%; text-align:center; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate data for <a href="/wiki/Arviat_Airport" title="Arviat Airport">Arviat Airport</a>, 1981&#8211;2010 normals, extremes 1973&#8211;present\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Month\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jan\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Feb\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Mar\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Apr\n</th>\n<th scope="col">May\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jun\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jul\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Aug\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Sep\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Oct\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Nov\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Dec\n</th>\n<th scope="col" style="border-left-width:medium">Year\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="text-align: center;">\n<th scope="row" style="height: 16px;">Record high &#176;C (&#176;F)\n</th>\n<td style="background: #DEDEFF; color:#FFFFFF; border-left-width:medium">73.7\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environment_Canada" title="Environment Canada">Environment Canada</a> Canadian Climate Normals 1981&#8211;2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccn_2_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-ccn_2-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Waters">Waters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Waters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HudsonBay.MODIS.2005may21.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="687" data-file-width="540" decoding="async" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/HudsonBay.MODIS.2005may21.jpg/220px-HudsonBay.MODIS.2005may21.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/HudsonBay.MODIS.2005may21.jpg/330px-HudsonBay.MODIS.2005may21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/HudsonBay.MODIS.2005may21.jpg/440px-HudsonBay.MODIS.2005may21.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HudsonBay.MODIS.2005may21.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In late spring (May), large chunks of ice float near the eastern shore of the bay, while the center of the bay remains frozen to the west. Between 1971 and 2007, the length of the ice-free season increased by about seven days in the southwestern part of the Hudson Bay, historically the last area to thaw.</div></div></div>\n<p>Hudson Bay has a lower average <a href="/wiki/Salinity" title="Salinity">salinity</a> level than that of ocean water. The main causes are the low rate of evaporation (the bay is ice-covered for much of the year), the large volume of <a href="/wiki/Surface_runoff" title="Surface runoff">terrestrial runoff</a> entering the bay (about 700&#160;km<sup>3</sup> (170&#160;cu&#160;mi) annually, the Hudson Bay watershed covering much of Canada, many rivers and streams discharging into the bay), and the limited connection with the Atlantic Ocean and its higher salinity. <a href="/wiki/Sea_ice" title="Sea ice">Sea ice</a> is about three times the annual river flow into the bay, and its annual <a href="/wiki/Freezing" title="Freezing">freezing</a> and thawing significantly alters the salinity of the surface layer.\n</p><p>One consequence of the lower salinity of the bay is that the <a href="/wiki/Melting_point" title="Melting point">freezing point</a> of the water is higher than in the rest of the world\'s oceans, thus decreasing the time that the bay remains ice-free.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shores">Shores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Shores">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The western shores of the bay are a lowland known as the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay_Lowlands" title="Hudson Bay Lowlands">Hudson Bay Lowlands</a> which covers 324,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (125,000&#160;sq&#160;mi). The area is drained by a large number of rivers and has formed a characteristic vegetation known as <a href="/wiki/Muskeg" title="Muskeg">muskeg</a>. Much of the landform has been shaped by the actions of <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a> and the shrinkage of the bay over long periods of time. Signs of numerous former beachfronts can be seen far inland from the current shore. A large portion of the lowlands in the province of Ontario is part of the <a href="/wiki/Polar_Bear_Provincial_Park" title="Polar Bear Provincial Park">Polar Bear Provincial Park</a>, and a similar portion of the lowlands in Manitoba is contained in <a href="/wiki/Wapusk_National_Park" title="Wapusk National Park">Wapusk National Park</a>, the latter location being a significant <a href="/wiki/Polar_bear" title="Polar bear">polar bear</a> <a href="/wiki/Maternity_den" title="Maternity den">maternity denning</a> area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In contrast, most of the eastern shores (the Quebec portion) form the western edge of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">Canadian Shield</a> in Quebec. The area is rocky and hilly. Its vegetation is typically <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">boreal forest</a>, and to the north, <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a>.\n</p><p>Measured by shoreline, Hudson Bay is the largest bay in the world (the largest in area being the Bay of Bengal).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands">Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are many islands in Hudson Bay, mostly near the eastern coast. All, as are the islands in James Bay, are part of the territory Nunavut and several are disputed by the Cree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> One group of islands is the <a href="/wiki/Belcher_Islands" title="Belcher Islands">Belcher Islands</a>. Another group includes the <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_Islands" title="Ottawa Islands">Ottawa Islands</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Hudson Bay occupies a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basin_(geology)" title="Basin (geology)">structural basin</a>, known as the <b>Hudson Bay basin</b>, that lies within the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">Canadian Shield</a>.  The collection and interpretation of outcrop, seismic and drillhole data for <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">exploration for oil and gas reservoirs</a> within the Hudson Bay basin found that it is filled by, at most, 2,500 meters (8,200&#160;ft) of <a href="/wiki/Ordovician" title="Ordovician">Ordovician</a> to <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a> <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolomite" title="Dolomite">dolomites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evaporite" title="Evaporite">evaporites</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_shale" title="Black shale">black shales</a>, and various <a href="/wiki/Clastic_rock" title="Clastic rock">clastic</a> <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">sedimentary rocks</a> that overlie less than 60 meters (200&#160;ft) of <a href="/wiki/Cambrian" title="Cambrian">Cambrian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strata" title="Strata">strata</a> that consist of unfossiliferous <a href="/wiki/Quartz_arenite" title="Quartz arenite">quartz sandstones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(geology)" title="Conglomerate (geology)">conglomerates</a>, overlain by <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sandy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stromatolite" title="Stromatolite">stromatolitic</a> <a href="/wiki/Dolostone" title="Dolostone">dolostones</a>. In addition, a minor amount of terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fluvial" title="Fluvial">fluvial</a> <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gravel" title="Gravel">gravels</a> are preserved in the fills of a ring of <a href="/wiki/Sinkhole" title="Sinkhole">sinkholes</a> created by the dissolution of <a href="/wiki/Silurian" title="Silurian">Silurian</a> evaporites during the Cretaceous Period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burgess2008a_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burgess2008a-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LavoieOthers2015a_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-LavoieOthers2015a-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roksandic1987a_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roksandic1987a-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SanfordOthers1998a_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-SanfordOthers1998a-39">[39]</a></sup>\n</p><p>From the large quantity of published geologic data that has been collected as the result of <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">hydrocarbon exploration</a>, academic research, and related <a href="/wiki/Geologic_map" title="Geologic map">geologic mapping</a>, a detailed history of the Hudson Bay basin has been reconstructed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LavoieOthers2015a_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-LavoieOthers2015a-37">[37]</a></sup> During the majority of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambrian_Period" title="Cambrian Period">Cambrian Period</a>, this basin did not exist. Rather, this part of the Canadian Shield area was still topographically high and emergent. It was only during the later part of the Cambrian that the rising sea level of the <a href="/wiki/Sauk_sequence" title="Sauk sequence">Sauk</a> <a href="/wiki/Marine_transgression" title="Marine transgression">marine transgression</a> slowly submerged it. During the Ordovician, this part of the Canadian Shield continued to be submerged by rising sea levels except for a brief middle Ordovician <a href="/wiki/Marine_regression" title="Marine regression">marine regression</a>. Only starting in the Late Ordovician and continuing into the Silurian did the gradual regional <a href="/wiki/Subsidence" title="Subsidence">subsidence</a> of this part of the Canadian Shield form the Hudson Bay basin. The formation of this basin resulted in the accumulation of black <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bituminous" title="Bituminous">bituminous</a> <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">oil shale</a> and evaporite deposits within its center, thick basin-margin limestone and dolomite, and the  development of extensive <a href="/wiki/Reef" title="Reef">reefs</a> that ringed the basin margins that were <a href="/wiki/Tectonic_uplift" title="Tectonic uplift">tectonically uplifted</a> as the basin subsided. During Middle Silurian times, subsidence ceased and this basin was uplifted. It generated an emergent arch, on which reefs grew, that divided the basin into eastern and western sub-basins. During the Devonian Period, this basin filled with terrestrial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_bed" title="Red bed">red beds</a> that interfinger with marine limestone and dolomites. Before deposition was terminated by marine regression, Upper Devonian black bituminous shale accumulated in the south-east of the basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burgess2008a_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Burgess2008a-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LavoieOthers2015a_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-LavoieOthers2015a-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roksandic1987a_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Roksandic1987a-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SanfordOthers1998a_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-SanfordOthers1998a-39">[39]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The remaining history of the Hudson Bay basin is largely unknown as a major <a href="/wiki/Unconformity" title="Unconformity">unconformity</a> separates Upper Devonian strata from <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> <a href="/wiki/Glacial_period" title="Glacial period">glacial deposits</a>. Except for poorly known terrestrial Cretaceous fluvial sands and gravels that are preserved as the fills of a ring of sinkholes around the center of this basin, strata representing this period of time are absent from the Hudson Bay basin and the surrounding Canadian Shield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burgess2008a_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-Burgess2008a-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SanfordOthers1998a_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-SanfordOthers1998a-39">[39]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Precambrian Shield underlying Hudson Bay and in which Hudson Bay basin formed is composed of two <a href="/wiki/Archean" title="Archean">Archean</a> proto-continents, the <a href="/wiki/Churchill_Craton" title="Churchill Craton">Western Churchill</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superior_craton" title="Superior craton">Superior cratons</a>. These <a href="/wiki/Craton" title="Craton">cratons</a> are separated by a tectonic collage that forms a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suture_zone" title="Suture zone">suture zone</a> between these cratons and the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Hudson_orogeny" title="Trans-Hudson orogeny">Trans-Hudson Orogen</a>. The Western Churchill and Superior cratons collided at about 1.9&#8211;1.8 Ga in the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Hudson_orogeny" title="Trans-Hudson orogeny">Trans-Hudson orogeny</a>. Because of the irregular shapes of the colliding cratons, this collision trapped between them large fragments of juvenile crust, a sizable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microcontinent" title="Microcontinent">microcontinent</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Island_arc" title="Island arc">island arc</a> <a href="/wiki/Terrane" title="Terrane">terranes</a>, beneath what is now the center of modern Hudson Bay as part of the Trans-Hudson Orogen. The Belcher islands are the eroded surface of the Belcher Fold Belt, which formed as a result of the tectonic compression and folding of sediments that accumulated along the margin of the Superior craton before its collision with the Western Churchill craton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DarbyshireOthers2010a_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-DarbyshireOthers2010a-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EatonOthers2010a_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-EatonOthers2010a-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PGR_Paulson2007_Rate_of_Lithospheric_Uplift_due_to_post-glacial_rebound.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1544" data-file-width="2038" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/PGR_Paulson2007_Rate_of_Lithospheric_Uplift_due_to_post-glacial_rebound.png/220px-PGR_Paulson2007_Rate_of_Lithospheric_Uplift_due_to_post-glacial_rebound.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/PGR_Paulson2007_Rate_of_Lithospheric_Uplift_due_to_post-glacial_rebound.png/330px-PGR_Paulson2007_Rate_of_Lithospheric_Uplift_due_to_post-glacial_rebound.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/PGR_Paulson2007_Rate_of_Lithospheric_Uplift_due_to_post-glacial_rebound.png/440px-PGR_Paulson2007_Rate_of_Lithospheric_Uplift_due_to_post-glacial_rebound.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PGR_Paulson2007_Rate_of_Lithospheric_Uplift_due_to_post-glacial_rebound.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of post-glacial rebound. Hudson Bay is in the region of the most rapid uplift.</div></div></div>\n<p>Hudson Bay and the associated structural basin lies within the center of a large <a href="/wiki/Free-air_gravity_anomaly" title="Free-air gravity anomaly">free-air gravity anomaly</a> that lies within the Canadian Shield. The similarity in areal extent of the free-air gravity anomaly with the perimeter of the former <a href="/wiki/Laurentide_Ice_Sheet" title="Laurentide Ice Sheet">Laurentide Ice Sheet</a> that covered this part of <a href="/wiki/Laurentia" title="Laurentia">Laurentia</a> led to a long-held conclusion that this perturbation in the Earth&#8217;s gravity reflected still ongoing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glacial_isostatic_adjustment" title="Glacial isostatic adjustment">glacial isostatic adjustment</a> to the melting and disappearance of this ice sheet. Data collected over Canada by the <a href="/wiki/Gravity_Recovery_and_Climate_Experiment" title="Gravity Recovery and Climate Experiment">Gravity Recovery and Climate Experiment</a> (GRACE) <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a> mission allowed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geophysicist" title="Geophysicist">geophysicists</a> to isolate the gravity signal associated with glacial isostatic adjustment from longer&#8211;time scale process of <a href="/wiki/Mantle_convection" title="Mantle convection">mantle convection</a> occurring beneath the Canadian Shield. Based upon this data, geophysicists and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth_scientist" title="Earth scientist">Earth scientists</a> concluded that the Laurentide Ice Sheet was composed of two large domes to the west and east of Hudson Bay. Modeling glacial isostatic adjustment using the GRACE data, they concluded that ~25 to ~45% of the observed free-air gravity anomaly was due to ongoing glacial isostatic adjustment, and the remainder likely represents longer time-scale effects of mantle convection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TamisieaOthers2007a_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-TamisieaOthers2007a-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Earth scientists have disagreed about what created the semicircular feature known as the <b><a href="/wiki/Nastapoka_arc" title="Nastapoka arc">Nastapoka arc</a></b> that forms a section of the shoreline of southeastern Hudson Bay. Noting the paucity of impact structures on Earth in relation to the Moon and Mars, Beals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beals1968a_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beals1968a-43">[43]</a></sup>  proposed that it is possibly part of a Precambrian extraterrestrial impact structure that is comparable in size to the <a href="/wiki/Mare_Crisium" title="Mare Crisium">Mare Crisium</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a>. In the same volume, Wilson<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilson1968a_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson1968a-44">[44]</a></sup> commented on Beals\' interpretation and alternately proposed that the Nastapoka arc may have formed as part of an extensive Precambrian continental collisional orogen, linked to the closure of an ancient ocean basin. The current general consensus is that it is an arcuate boundary of tectonic origin between the Belcher Fold Belt and undeformed basement of the Superior craton created during the Trans-Hudson orogeny.  This is because no credible evidence for such an <a href="/wiki/Impact_structure" title="Impact structure">impact structure</a> has been found by regional magnetic, <a href="/wiki/Bouguer_anomaly" title="Bouguer anomaly">Bouguer gravity</a>, and other geologic studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DarbyshireOthers2010a_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-DarbyshireOthers2010a-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EatonOthers2010a_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-EatonOthers2010a-41">[41]</a></sup> However, other Earth scientists have proposed that the evidence of an Archean impact might have been masked by deformation accompanying the later formation of the Trans-Hudson orogen and regard an impact origin as a plausible possibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GoodingOthers1992a_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-GoodingOthers1992a-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BleekerOthers2004a_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-BleekerOthers2004a-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arctic_Bridge">Arctic Bridge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Arctic Bridge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arctic_Routes_(RUS).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1267" data-file-width="1010" decoding="async" height="276" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Arctic_Routes_%28RUS%29.svg/220px-Arctic_Routes_%28RUS%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Arctic_Routes_%28RUS%29.svg/330px-Arctic_Routes_%28RUS%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Arctic_Routes_%28RUS%29.svg/440px-Arctic_Routes_%28RUS%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arctic_Routes_(RUS).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Arctic Bridge <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shipping_route" title="Shipping route">shipping route</a> (blue line) is hoped to link North America to <a href="/wiki/Market_(economics)" title="Market (economics)">markets</a> in Europe and Asia using ice-free routes across the Arctic Ocean</div></div></div>\n<p>The longer periods of ice-free navigation and the reduction of Arctic Ocean ice coverage have led to Russian and Canadian interest in the potential for commercial trade routes across the Arctic and into Hudson Bay. The so-called <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Bridge" title="Arctic Bridge">Arctic Bridge</a> would link Churchill, Manitoba, and the Russian port of <a href="/wiki/Murmansk" title="Murmansk">Murmansk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coastal_communities">Coastal communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Coastal communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Hudson+Bay%22" rel="nofollow">"Hudson Bay"</a>&#160;&#8211;&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Hudson+Bay%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">news</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Hudson+Bay%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Hudson+Bay%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Hudson+Bay%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Hudson+Bay%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The coast of Hudson Bay is extremely sparsely populated; there are only about a dozen communities. Some of these were founded as trading posts in the 17th and 18th centuries by the Hudson\'s Bay Company, making them some of the oldest settlements in <a href="/wiki/Western_Canada" title="Western Canada">Western Canada</a>. With the closure of the HBC posts and stores, although many are now run by <a href="/wiki/The_North_West_Company" title="The North West Company">The North West Company</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> in the second half of the 20th century, many coastal villages are now almost exclusively populated by <a href="/wiki/Cree" title="Cree">Cree</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> people. Two main historic sites along the coast were <a href="/wiki/York_Factory" title="York Factory">York Factory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales_Fort" title="Prince of Wales Fort">Prince of Wales Fort</a>.\n</p><p>Communities along the Hudson Bay coast or on islands in the bay are (all populations are as of 2016):\n</p>\n<ul><li>Nunavut\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Arviat" title="Arviat">Arviat</a>, population 2,657</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_Inlet,_Nunavut" title="Chesterfield Inlet, Nunavut">Chesterfield Inlet</a>, population 437</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Coral_Harbour" title="Coral Harbour">Coral Harbour</a>, population 891</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rankin_Inlet" title="Rankin Inlet">Rankin Inlet</a>, population 2,842</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sanikiluaq" title="Sanikiluaq">Sanikiluaq</a>, population 882</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Whale_Cove,_Nunavut" title="Whale Cove, Nunavut">Whale Cove</a>, population 435</li></ul></li>\n<li>Manitoba\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Churchill,_Manitoba" title="Churchill, Manitoba">Churchill</a>, population 899</li></ul></li>\n<li>Ontario\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Severn_First_Nation" title="Fort Severn First Nation">Fort Severn First Nation</a>, population 334</li></ul></li>\n<li>Quebec\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Akulivik" title="Akulivik">Akulivik</a>, population 633</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inukjuak" title="Inukjuak">Inukjuak</a>, population 1,757</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kuujjuarapik" title="Kuujjuarapik">Kuujjuarapik</a>, population 686</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puvirnituq" title="Puvirnituq">Puvirnituq</a>, population 1,779</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Umiujaq" title="Umiujaq">Umiujaq</a>, population 442</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Whapmagoostui" title="Whapmagoostui">Whapmagoostui</a>, population 984</li></ul></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_development">Military development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Military development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Hudson\'s Bay Company built forts as fur trade strongholds against the French or other possible invaders. One example is <a href="/wiki/York_Factory" title="York Factory">York Factory</a> with angled walls to help defend the fort. In the 1950s, during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, a few sites along the coast became part of the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Canada_Line" title="Mid-Canada Line">Mid-Canada Line</a>, watching for a potential Soviet bomber attack over the North Pole. The only Arctic deep-water port in Canada is the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Churchill" title="Port of Churchill">Port of Churchill</a>, located at Churchill, Manitoba.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Great_Recycling_and_Northern_Development_Canal" title="Great Recycling and Northern Development Canal">Great Recycling and Northern Development Canal</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lake_Agassiz" title="Lake Agassiz">Lake Agassiz</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Hudson_Bay_rivers" title="List of Hudson Bay rivers">List of Hudson Bay rivers</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tyrrell_Sea" title="Tyrrell Sea">Tyrrell Sea</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hudson_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="https://www.britannica.com/place/Hudson-Bay" rel="nofollow">Hudson Bay | sea, Canada | Britannica.com</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://www.wissenladen.de/maps/map.php?Canada_(Hudson_Bay)&amp;id=72&amp;ln=en" rel="nofollow">Wissenladen.de</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-atlas-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-atlas_3-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://atlas.nrcan.gc.ca/site/english/maps/archives/5thedition/environment/water/mcr4055" rel="nofollow">"Canada Drainage Basins"</a>. <i>The National Atlas of Canada, 5th edition</i>.
